    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9800739839226426058"><b>This revolutionary, award-winning play by a lauded playwright and poet is a fearless portrayal of the experiences of women of color—“extraordinary and wonderful…that anyone can relate to” (<i>The New York Times</i>) and continues to move and resonate with readers today more than ever.</b><br/><br/>From its inception in California in 1974 to its highly acclaimed critical success at Joseph Papp'</span>
  <span id="freeText9800739839226426058" style="display:none"><b>This revolutionary, award-winning play by a lauded playwright and poet is a fearless portrayal of the experiences of women of color—“extraordinary and wonderful…that anyone can relate to” (<i>The New York Times</i>) and continues to move and resonate with readers today more than ever.</b><br /><br />From its inception in California in 1974 to its highly acclaimed critical success at Joseph Papp's Public Theater and on Broadway, the Obie Award-winning <i>for colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf</i> has excited, inspired, and transformed audiences all over the country. Passionate and fearless, Shange's words reveal what it is to be of color and female in the twentieth century. First published in 1975 when it was praised by The New Yorker for "encompassing...every feeling and experience a woman has ever had," <i>for colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf</i> will be read and performed for generations to come. Here is the complete text, with stage directions, of a groundbreaking dramatic prose poem written in vivid and powerful language that resonates with unusual beauty in its fierce message to the world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9800739839226426058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/39210677-marilyn-basel"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1493826812i/39210677._UX100_CR0,24,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/39210677-marilyn-basel">Marilyn Basel</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is for the time it was written a bold affirmation that male dominance at the emotional and physical expense of females is not acceptable. The spe<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is for the time it was written a bold affirmation that male dominance at the emotional and physical expense of females is not acceptable. The spectacle of Cookie slapping men around on TV's Empire is a travesty compared to the courage voiced in this book. I read it aloud to men doing life in prison inside State Prison of Southern Michigan back in the early 80s when teaching for Spring Arbor College. They were sitting lower and farther back in their chairs as I read. Not just one of them changed how they saw relationships with women after that. Until the gender wars are ended in a bloodless revolution resulting in mutual respect in relationships without dominance games, this book should be read aloud to your daughters to prepare them for the realities of life.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/648367-what-was-the-main-struggle-in-the-book">What was the main struggle in the book from your perspective?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_648367'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F58098.For_Colored_Girls_Who_Have_Considered_Suicide_When_the_Rainbow_Is_Enuf">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/648367-what-was-the-main-struggle-in-the-book">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/648367-what-was-the-main-struggle-in-the-book">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/51749902-tania-s"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/51749902-tania-s">Tania S</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Literary Essay:For Colored Girls Tania Smith<br/> <br/><br/> “ For colored Girls” and the author is NTozake Shange. NTozake is a renowned playwright her work include<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Literary Essay:For Colored Girls Tania Smith<br /> <br /><br /> “ For colored Girls” and the author is NTozake Shange. NTozake is a renowned playwright her work include some sing, some cry, which she wrote with four other writers. She is a graduate of Barnard and recipient of a master’s in American Studies from the University of Southern California, she lives in Brooklyn. “For Colored Girls” setting is in Brooklyn with multiple women who have different difficulties in their life. The black African American women have overcame challenges that happens to be too hard for others to overcome. NTozake Shange uses symbolism, personification, and similes to show how much colored girls go through and how they get through it all everyday without complaining of having a fit. <br /><br /> NTozake Shange uses symbolism to show how the music to her is describing a way of life and how people's lives are. It describes the sounds that is being portrayed from her point of view and how the music expresses thoughts and emotions.The way of life is being described as hard and not easy as a For Colored Girl in the south. The symbolism that is given is, “ But sing her rhythms/carin/struggle/hard times sing her song of life. She been dead so long,closed in silence so long,she doesn't know the sound of her own voice, her infinite beauty” (17) <br /><br /> In “For Colored Girls” NTozake Shange uses personification to describe how people are looking at her since she got an abortion. Her outlook on the world is different now and so is her circle, people stop being friends with her because of a decision she decided to make : Her world has changed due to the fact that she is bring life to the world, she too is ashamed of the decision that was made and now she has to deal with it. The sentence in the book says, “eyes crawling up one me eyes rollin in my thighs metal horses gnawin my womb dead mice fall from my mouth” (36) <br /><br /> NTozake Shange creates a simile comparing good and bad love The women and her sister realized how much good love stood between them and that this would be the first time she had this moment. Every since she found out about a colored girl she tried to not be that and left bitter in somebody else’s cup. She described it like this, “come to somebody to love me without deep &amp; nasty repetition scald from lye or being left screaming in a street full of lunatica/ whisperin slut bitch bitch niggah/ get outta my face with alla that.”(56).<br /><br /> NTozake Shange uses symbolism, personification, and similes to show how much colored girls go through and how they get through it all everyday without complaining of having a fit. I used text evidence to show how the girls struggle and the reaction they get from people when they try to do better with themselves. If you was one of these girls how would you feel if somebody summarized your whole life in a book? Would you feel that the author is not being appropriate or would of you thank her for showing people what life is all about in a African American young lady?’ If said you would thank her explain why.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_149162066" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149162066" />
    <a title="Kei As in Keisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1759418-kei-as-in-keisha"><img alt="Kei As in Keisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605695313p2/1759418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149162066?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kei As in Keisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kei As in Keisha" href="/user/show/1759418-kei-as-in-keisha">Kei As in Keisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1759418-kei-as-in-keisha?shelf=books-i-despise">books-i-despise</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer149162066&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer149162066" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7152694432478394232">[EDITED TO CLARIFY A FEW THINGS]<br/><br/>I thoroughly understand poetic license and the art of using vernacular in literature. Langston Hughes has taught me well. ;-)<br/><br/><br/>February, 2011<br/>This book is not a novel. It is a choreopoem of fictional stories told by characters who all represent a color worn, i.e. Lady in Red, Lady in Yellow, Lady in Purple, etc. The title alone being the first clue, this is also not a timeless piece. I’ll just get right to why I give this book one star. I despise intentional misspell</span>
  <span id="freeText7152694432478394232" style="display:none">[EDITED TO CLARIFY A FEW THINGS]<br /><br />I thoroughly understand poetic license and the art of using vernacular in literature. Langston Hughes has taught me well. ;-)<br /><br /><br />February, 2011<br />This book is not a novel. It is a choreopoem of fictional stories told by characters who all represent a color worn, i.e. Lady in Red, Lady in Yellow, Lady in Purple, etc. The title alone being the first clue, this is also not a timeless piece. I’ll just get right to why I give this book one star. I despise intentional misspellings of words. It is one of my more severe pet peeves. I never wanted to read this book in the past because seeing the word “enough” spelled “enuf” irked me tremendously. Throughout the book, all of the poems are told in broken English (because that's obviously the only way to hear a black voice in literature) and lots of words are either misspelled or not spelled at all, for example, “could” is spelled “cd.” <br /><br />There is an art to capturing the true voice of a character; and if that character is "ill-spoken," then there is a way to transfer that voice and still have it flow nicely as words on a page. I didn't like the way it was done in this piece; however there are many [BLACK] authors who have mastered this technique and have done so beautifully and provocatively -- and not just for the sake of showing a character's inability otherwise.<br /><br />I don’t like the word “colored” to describe a person. I don’t respect the idea of taking an oppressive word and capitalizing off of it; and capitalizing off of the grief that accompanies the word’s connotation. Apparently, there are only a few stories to tell about "colored girls" and, given the collections of books available to the masses that are along the same order; those stories are all disgusting and sad. These colored girls are tormented souls and maybe they’re so tormented because they refer to and see themselves as “colored,” because honestly, I must profess that being a black woman is really not that big of a deal. In fact, <b> I quite enjoy it and don’t see my skin color as a direct attachment to all things sorrowful, painful, diseased, abused, and oppressed.</b> The book’s title says “For Colored Girls,” but perhaps, this book is not for me. I am not saying my personal life has been all sunshine, lollipops, and rainbows, but how many people of ANY shade can say that about their own lives?<br /> <br />“But this is real." I know, I know... and my response to that is this: Women, if this is what you’re constantly attaching yourselves to, then you allow it to become your stigma, thus YOUR reality. Women... WOMEN go through this, NOT just “colored” women. There are so many women who will read these poems and relate to everything except the skin tone. So why is it that some authors have chosen to make universal experiences exclusive to one race and one sex? ”Sing a black girl’s song!” Let’s keep our sorrow alive and let the world cry with us. And then what? We hope that "colored girls" who are actually not children, but grown women, will make better decisions in life? Will they go to college, use birth control and condoms, and stop dating guys named "Beaux Willie?" <br /><br />People really don't care about this being "real." They read it, say "ooh that's so sad" and go on sipping their lattes, while we stay and fight the preconceived stigmas... the same stories told in various forms of mass media over and over again until one image is indelibly printed in the minds of the masses. <br /><br />In addition to the aforementioned, main foibles, many of the characters needed to take responsibility for their own poor choices in the scenarios, yet they failed to do so in their own deliveries. For example, the characters Beaux Willie and Crystal, Crystal tells the story. She had been with Beaux Willie since she was thirteen years old. He went away to war and returned crazy and abusive. He was also jobless. Together, they had two children and she worked to support him and her children. At some point, Beaux Willie decided he wanted to marry Crystal, who suddenly realized that she shouldn’t marry him. He was no longer good enough. She told him this while calling him all kinds of names including the <b> N-word. </b> So... he took her children and dangled them out of an open window five stories high. He asked her if she loved him and if so, will she marry him? And Crystal whispered a response... Listen... [Anyone with the smallest dose of common sense knows that you should always go along with crazy people. Tell them whatever they want to hear until they calm down and step out of their moment of craziness]. Well, Beaux Willie didn't like whatever she whispered and in response, he dropped the kids out of the window. He murdered their children. <br /><br />And this is what everyone is calling realistic? Can it happen? Yeah, I’m sure it can, but I don’t know a black woman on this planet who would have allowed that to happen without a knife being jabbed deep into Beaux Willie’s back. The children wouldn’t have been the only ones murdered that day. <br /><br />I am also disgusted by the people on the street who stood there and watched the children dangling from the window. No one thought to run into their own house and grab a mattress or something huge and soft for the kids to land on? Or no one thought to gather around underneath where they were hanging, to at least try to catch them? This could have prevented their death and maybe they would have only ended up with twisted ankles or a broken arm.<br /><br />And so these are the reasons why I do not love this piece. When a fictional story contains extreme, unbelievable, preventive stupidity, I am impatient and completely unsympathetic towards the characters. I am not bribed into feeling emotionally attached simply because I am massivley told that I should be, since I am "of color."</span>
  <a data-text-id="7152694432478394232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3299231161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3299231161" />
    <a title="Jenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna"><img alt="Jenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535136437p2/3536004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3299231161?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenna" href="/user/show/3536004-jenna">Jenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=race">race</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3536004-jenna?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3299231161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11102823671468773314">If there is ever a time in the future when people are able to gather together in groups again, I want to see a performance of <i>For colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf</i>. <br/><br/>It is beautiful, passionate, real, gritty, lyrical. I felt like I was reading a song. <br/><br/>It's a poem performed by 7 women, each one of them representing a colour of the rainbow, and one the colour brown. They speak of their experiences as Black women, their dreams and their sorrows. Of abortion and AIDS </span>
  <span id="freeText11102823671468773314" style="display:none">If there is ever a time in the future when people are able to gather together in groups again, I want to see a performance of <i>For colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf</i>. <br /><br />It is beautiful, passionate, real, gritty, lyrical. I felt like I was reading a song. <br /><br />It's a poem performed by 7 women, each one of them representing a colour of the rainbow, and one the colour brown. They speak of their experiences as Black women, their dreams and their sorrows. Of abortion and AIDS and abandonment. Of rape and racism. Of longing and love, racism and violence. <br /><br />It is written in the women's vernacular which adds a rich and authentic element to the poem. I won't claim to have "gotten" all the layers of meaning, but I will claim that I enjoyed it very much. And maybe I can't see the performance right now, but I'm glad I could at least read the book.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12477785454992109550">The ish. A pivotal work in theatre. I once heard Ntozake Shange explain that one of her goals as a writer was to break down the English language, to undo, redo, replay, and rework the English language, in such a way that its power for white supremacist goals and idea transfer would be rendered useless. Now that's all types of deep - this idea that language can teach us destruction and prejudice and by deconstructing that language those who have been oppressed can reclaim and enter into the very </span>
  <span id="freeText12477785454992109550" style="display:none">The ish. A pivotal work in theatre. I once heard Ntozake Shange explain that one of her goals as a writer was to break down the English language, to undo, redo, replay, and rework the English language, in such a way that its power for white supremacist goals and idea transfer would be rendered useless. Now that's all types of deep - this idea that language can teach us destruction and prejudice and by deconstructing that language those who have been oppressed can reclaim and enter into the very language that had formerly been exclusive - creating something new entirely.<br /><br />This sentiment reminds me a great deal of the book Rolling the R's which also complicates and obliterates ideas of language, grammar, and syntax.<br /><br />I love reading this while listening to Nina Simone - particularly Four Women. </span>

<div id="review_3136301742" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3136301742" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4643325-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535048395p2/4643325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3136301742?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/4643325-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4643325-paul?shelf=reading-women-bingo-2020">reading-women-bingo-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3136301742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2283764760953345525">This is a choreopoem and is a series of twenty poems for a cast of seven principals: they are Ladies in Red, Orange, Yellow, Green, Blue, Purple and Brown. It expresses the struggles and problems that African-American women face; and amazingly it’s 45 years old now. The poems are linked by music. Subjects addressed include rape, domestic violence, loss, abortion and being abandoned. This is based on Shange’s own experience. <br/>I have read this rather than seen a production of it and obviously it wo</span>
  <span id="freeText2283764760953345525" style="display:none">This is a choreopoem and is a series of twenty poems for a cast of seven principals: they are Ladies in Red, Orange, Yellow, Green, Blue, Purple and Brown. It expresses the struggles and problems that African-American women face; and amazingly it’s 45 years old now. The poems are linked by music. Subjects addressed include rape, domestic violence, loss, abortion and being abandoned. This is based on Shange’s own experience. <br />I have read this rather than seen a production of it and obviously it would be much more powerful on stage. There is a film as well which I also haven’t seen, but will look out for.<br />There is so much in this and Shange dissects the relationship between black women and black men as well as looking at how black women are portrayed:<br />“ever since i realized there waz someone callt<br />a colored girl an evil woman a bitch or a nag<br />i been trying not to be that &amp; leave bitterness<br />in somebody else’s cup”<br />Shange’s candour has been criticized for highlighting this issue, but she is clear what her focus is:<br />“sing a black girl’s song<br />bring her out<br />to know herself<br />to know you<br />but sing her rhythms<br />care/struggle/hard times<br />sing her song of life<br />she’s been dead so long<br />closed in silence so long<br />she doesn’t know the sound of her own voice<br />her infinite beauty”<br />Shange also says what she has to say with a deal of humour as well:<br />“without any assistance or guidance from you<br />i have loved you assiduously for 8 months 2 wks &amp; a day<br />i have been stood up four times<br />i've left 7 packages on yr doorstep<br />forty poems 2 plants &amp; 3 handmade notecards i left<br />town so i cd send to you have been no help to me<br />on my job<br />you call at 3:00 in the mornin on weekdays<br />so i cd drive 27 1/2 miles cross the bay before i go to work<br />charmin charmin<br />but you are of no assistance<br />i want you to know<br />this waz an experiment<br />to see how selifsh i cd be<br />if i wd really carry on to snare a possible lover<br />if i waz capable of debasin my self for the love of another<br />if i cd stand not being wanted<br />when i wanted to be wanted<br />&amp; i cannot<br />so<br />with no further assistance &amp; no guidance from you<br />i am endin this affair<br /><br />this note is attached to a plant<br />i've been waterin since the day i met you<br />you may water it<br />yr damn self”<br />Shange grew up in the midst of the civil rights movement and the turbulence of the 1960s and it shows in this; she is making a point not just to black men, but to the white feminist movement as well. There is a pattern of frustration as well; an alienation and loneliness because issues with black men. There has been an ongoing debate surrounding this which has been well documented. <br />It was also interesting to see a walk on part for Toussaint L’Overture. <br />This is a powerful piece of work with many layers and a powerful and significant message. I hope to see it on stage one day; but in the meantime I will look out for the film.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2283764760953345525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128957514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128957514" />
    <a title="Charlie Ramirez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4228181-charlie-ramirez"><img alt="Charlie Ramirez" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128957514?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlie Ramirez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlie Ramirez" href="/user/show/4228181-charlie-ramirez">Charlie Ramirez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128957514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9425582915323730792">For Colored Girls who Have Considered Suicide when the Rainbow is Enuf has been the most profound, interesting, mind- blowing books I have come across this year. This was my first time being introduced to a chore poem, which is simply a collection of poems that have been strategically put together into one novel. One thing I learned from Shange, the author, is the attention to the title of the book. Upon reading the first three words of the title, "For colored girls..." you assume that the word </span>
  <span id="freeText9425582915323730792" style="display:none">For Colored Girls who Have Considered Suicide when the Rainbow is Enuf has been the most profound, interesting, mind- blowing books I have come across this year. This was my first time being introduced to a chore poem, which is simply a collection of poems that have been strategically put together into one novel. One thing I learned from Shange, the author, is the attention to the title of the book. Upon reading the first three words of the title, "For colored girls..." you assume that the word colored pertains to their skin color, more specifically, black women. However, upon reading through the poems, none of the characters are known by name. They are simple labeled 'the lady in blue' or 'the lady in red'. Each girl is labeled by a color. Each color serves as a symbolic meaning for each girl. For example, the poem that contains the lady in red is suffering from domestic violence, which red serves as a metaphor. Largely unique for the style of the book, For Colored Girls may be one of my new favorite books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9425582915323730792" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer833842778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13301425143832848237">'coloured' (minoritised, othered in their skin, colonised OR vibrant, various, multifaceted) 'girls' (infantilised, sexually exploited and pathologised, excluded from woman/lady OR youthful, spirited, free, pure-hearted) , five Black women… speaking in the safe space of loving affirmation between them, poetising rawness of pain and beauty, passion and exhaustion...<br/><br/>No respectability politics. Don't start telling these women what they should have done. These are words of possibility and impossibil</span>
  <span id="freeText13301425143832848237" style="display:none">'coloured' (minoritised, othered in their skin, colonised OR vibrant, various, multifaceted) 'girls' (infantilised, sexually exploited and pathologised, excluded from woman/lady OR youthful, spirited, free, pure-hearted) , five Black women… speaking in the safe space of loving affirmation between them, poetising rawness of pain and beauty, passion and exhaustion...<br /><br />No respectability politics. Don't start telling these women what they should have done. These are words of possibility and impossibility. They did what was possible and cried for what was impossible<br /><br />Feminists are saying NOW what Shange says here about rape culture… (how strongly can I echo the words of Black feminists/womanists and say we White women have to hear Black women and get <i>behind</i> them on this, because not only are they hurt by male violence but by the violence of a law-and-order feminism that signifies on the plantation narrative of Black men as a threat to White women)<br /><br />Colour is sweetness here with bitter linings... is worn with glitter... orange butterflies and aqua sequins… on bodies glowing with femme charms to take their pleasure from men who can't be loved, men who hurt their hearts and utter cheap apologies, men who even destroy their lives. The nourishing saving love they live on is for each other. Shange's ladies in red brown blue purple yellow step from the stage leaving space for the queer coloured girls to dance their songs...<br /><br />I'm hoping to go see <a href="http://www.womensgrid.org.uk/groups/?p=1747" rel="nofollow noopener">a production</a> of this soon!<br /></span>

<div id="review_123089656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123089656" />
    <a title="Craig Cunningham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3946782-craig-cunningham"><img alt="Craig Cunningham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278201468p2/3946782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123089656?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig Cunningham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig Cunningham" href="/user/show/3946782-craig-cunningham">Craig Cunningham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123089656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14051574917630290459"><br/><br/>I read this book a million years ago.Well, to bespecific back in 1975, around the time of its original publication. However, I have read it several more times since then, and I have seen the Play performed more than five times. The play presents an overwhelming expereience that embraces the audience member in a cultural experience of the African American woman and other women in the African Diaspora. The reading of the text and the viewing of the original play present a sometimes bleek, daunting</span>
  <span id="freeText14051574917630290459" style="display:none"><br /><br />I read this book a million years ago.Well, to bespecific back in 1975, around the time of its original publication. However, I have read it several more times since then, and I have seen the Play performed more than five times. The play presents an overwhelming expereience that embraces the audience member in a cultural experience of the African American woman and other women in the African Diaspora. The reading of the text and the viewing of the original play present a sometimes bleek, daunting, view of life, but the expressive hope that looms through much of the poetry offers a vibrant potential for change. I really enjoy the book, because of the specifics with which Ntozake Shange approaches words. She is a wordsmith. She carefully sculpts, massages, and molds the words to create this tapestry of emotion and brilliance. Now that this textual call for revolution will be made into a motion picture, I pray that the original revolutionary, nationalist, feminist, and cultural paradigms in this piece shall not be exploited or removed to fit into a 21st century framework for a simple story wrapped up in a bow. I love this piece, and I really believe in theatre, this piece started a genre of pieces in the sixties and seventies in which characters speaking directly to the audience extolled their feelings, emotional wreckages, and depths of intensity through the catacombs of cultural examination. Another play, which does not have the same depth as Ms. Shange's work, is the Runaways, which was a Broadway production as well. I really enjoy works this this, and Ntozake Shange does fantastic work in this area. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14051574917630290459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_947892936" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/947892936" />
    <a title="Liz Janet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5114433-liz-janet"><img alt="Liz Janet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574021381p2/5114433.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/947892936?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz Janet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz Janet" href="/user/show/5114433-liz-janet">Liz Janet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer947892936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11483827955731934083">Read this before seeing the film, it is worth it. This play is one of the strongest stories about abuse and discrimination, from almost all aspects that I have had the great pleasure of reading.<br/><br/>I have seen many people criticize how the characters were represented, some even claiming that the characters could have taken more “responsibility” for what happened to them, and I am very sure that these people missed one of the messages of the story, that people are flawed, and that sometimes it is har</span>
  <span id="freeText11483827955731934083" style="display:none">Read this before seeing the film, it is worth it. This play is one of the strongest stories about abuse and discrimination, from almost all aspects that I have had the great pleasure of reading.<br /><br />I have seen many people criticize how the characters were represented, some even claiming that the characters could have taken more “responsibility” for what happened to them, and I am very sure that these people missed one of the messages of the story, that people are flawed, and that sometimes it is hard to leave. For example, someone criticized one of the characters who was being abused by her partner/husband physically and emotionally, and she stayed with him. This person said that she should just have left, but to abuse victims it is often not that easy. There is also an instance of a mother’s abuse towards her daughter, and this person said that she could once more leave and make her own fortune. I am now convinced that this person has no knowledge of abuse, economics, or the cultural upbringing some people are raised with.<br /><br />It is a very trigger filled play, so one must look at it with caution. My favourite part was the depiction of rape, including that even people we know can do it, rape is no longer a stranger in a dark alley, but ti can be a neighbour, someone we consider a best friend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11483827955731934083" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2067080453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067080453" />
    <a title="Bobbieshiann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39394999-bobbieshiann"><img alt="Bobbieshiann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496365582p2/39394999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067080453?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bobbieshiann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bobbieshiann" href="/user/show/39394999-bobbieshiann">Bobbieshiann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439186817" href="/book/show/8687650-for-colored-girls-who-have-considered-suicide-when-the-rainbow-is-enuf">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39394999-bobbieshiann?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39394999-bobbieshiann?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067080453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5293052200307255120">“Ever since i realized there waz someone callt a colored girl an evil woman a bitch or a nag i been tryin not to be that & leave bitterness in somebody else’s cup.”<br/><br/>My first read of 2020 is a journey that should not be taken lightly. A cheropoem that is for women, written by a woman, and be stopped by no one. Ntozake tells the story of 7 women who have endured sexism, rape, body shaming, racism, and more. These women are represented as colors of the rainbow and are connected as they put on a perf</span>
  <span id="freeText5293052200307255120" style="display:none">“Ever since i realized there waz someone callt a colored girl an evil woman a bitch or a nag i been tryin not to be that &amp; leave bitterness in somebody else’s cup.”<br /><br />My first read of 2020 is a journey that should not be taken lightly. A cheropoem that is for women, written by a woman, and be stopped by no one. Ntozake tells the story of 7 women who have endured sexism, rape, body shaming, racism, and more. These women are represented as colors of the rainbow and are connected as they put on a performance to display their pain. They show strength and bring awareness to what is hardly discussed in this time. They bring forth what it is to be a woman of color and I understand that there has been backlash for supposedly bashing men, but this is not for men and yet in this cheropoem, the women desire men and love them, and ache for that love to be returned. <br /><br />I now understand why this choreopoem has been carried on over the years. I am pretty sure we are familiar with Tyler Perry’s version of a For Colored Girls. You can picture the movie as your reading and it makes me applaud Ntozake for going against the norm and speaking so many women’s truth. For Colored Girls is ground breaking and does not end in sorrow. These women show strength and close with, “i found god in myself &amp; i love her/ i loved her fiercely.”<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5293052200307255120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1337732383?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337732383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11450433190232587554">I have to say that I loved this play. It was a bit weird to read the stage directions along with the poetry that was being said by these characters, but it was quite easy to read and follow.<br/><br/>For colored girls is considered a choreopoem (i.e. there are monologues that also include dance and music) with seven women in different colors speaking to the audience.<br/><br/>The seven women are the lady in red, lady in orange, lady in yellow, lady in green, lady in blue, lady in brown, and lady in purple.<br/><br/>Some of t</span>
  <span id="freeText11450433190232587554" style="display:none">I have to say that I loved this play. It was a bit weird to read the stage directions along with the poetry that was being said by these characters, but it was quite easy to read and follow.<br /><br />For colored girls is considered a choreopoem (i.e. there are monologues that also include dance and music) with seven women in different colors speaking to the audience.<br /><br />The seven women are the lady in red, lady in orange, lady in yellow, lady in green, lady in blue, lady in brown, and lady in purple.<br /><br />Some of the poems really spoke to me a lot and the play tackles so many different subjects such as rape, abortion, domestic violence. <br /><br />Some of the language was a bit harsh too. There were a lot of n words and some ethnic slurs in there too. I wouldn't recommend to those who may be easily offended and who may not want to read about some of the subjects of this play. <br /><br /><blockquote>lady in brown<br />&amp; this is for colored girls who have considered <br />suicide/but are movin to the ends of their own<br />rainbows</blockquote><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11450433190232587554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1764775324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764775324" />
    <a title="Aubrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey"><img alt="Aubrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1472535045p2/4119460.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1764775324?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aubrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aubrey" href="/user/show/4119460-aubrey">Aubrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780553229554" href="/book/show/294644.for_colored_girls_who_have_considered_suicide_when_the_rainbow_is_enuf">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=reality-check">reality-check</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=r-2019">r-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=person-of-reality">person-of-reality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=person-of-everything">person-of-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=1-read-on-hand">1-read-on-hand</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=shorty-short">shorty-short</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=antidote-think-twice-read">antidote-think-twice-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=antidote-think-twice-all">antidote-think-twice-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=r-goodreads">r-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4119460-aubrey?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764775324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5154962929354263170"><blockquote>
  <i>i loved you on purpose<br/>i was open on purpose<br/>i still crave vulnerability & close talk<br/>& i'm not even sorry bout you bein sorry<br/>you can carry all the guilt & grime ya wanna<br/>just dont give it to me<br/>i cant use another sorry<br/>next time<br/>you should admit<br/>you're mean/low-down/triflin/& no count straight out<br/>steada bein sorry all the time<br/>enjoy bein yrself</i>
</blockquote>3.5/5<br/><br/>I knew I was setting myself up for a less than complete experience by reading this play script rather than seeing the play performed, but after such a lo</span>
  <span id="freeText5154962929354263170" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>i loved you on purpose<br />i was open on purpose<br />i still crave vulnerability &amp; close talk<br />&amp; i'm not even sorry bout you bein sorry<br />you can carry all the guilt &amp; grime ya wanna<br />just dont give it to me<br />i cant use another sorry<br />next time<br />you should admit<br />you're mean/low-down/triflin/&amp; no count straight out<br />steada bein sorry all the time<br />enjoy bein yrself</i>
</blockquote>3.5/5<br /><br />I knew I was setting myself up for a less than complete experience by reading this play script rather than seeing the play performed, but after such a long school period of being trained on the reading of myriad Shakespeare plays, the comparatively inaccessible means of watching specific ones, whether filmed or live, leads me to choose to experience in whatever form I come first upon and worry about better means of exposure later. Plays don't get a lot of traction these days whether on GR or in real life, leastwise to my untutored gaze, so this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5517.A_Raisin_in_the_Sun" title="A Raisin in the Sun by Lorraine Hansberry" rel="nofollow noopener">A Raisin in the Sun</a> remain remarkable for being some of the best known examples outside of the Shakespearean monopoly, and how outside that monopoly the very structural fiber of this play is. It almost begs to be not seen or herd but witnessed, borderline liturgical in its confessions and damnations and revelations, even tending towards celebrations amongst the deprivations that continue to plague black womanhood near a half century later. My personal rating is helped by this comprehension as much as it is hindered by the form by which this choreopoem comes to me. A later, more holistic performance awaits, but when and by what means I will encounter it, I do not yet know.<br /><br />This work didn't really start coming together for me till the very end, and it ultimately left me somewhat moved but neither totally blown over or completely in hatred. There's a number of random Internet strangers I've recently come into contact with through a discord group who I know would throw conniptions over the choices of spelling and capitalization Shange makes, but I've read too much and too widely to still be bothered by such trivial nitpicking, so it wasn't the framing that interfered with as much as it was what came with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11337.The_Bluest_Eye" title="The Bluest Eye by Toni Morrison" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bluest Eye</a>, where I acknowledge that my personal experience and that of every white chick under the sun will forever lack the resources, nay, the paradigm needed to encounter this narrative of black womanhood and resonate with it in any way deeper than a murmur near completely superficial with its white washing. Fortunately, the average rating for this work is just fine and likely filled with the recognition of those who have actually seen this performed rather than merely the words on their pages, and as I am committed to accompanying my reading in the same manner, I'm not too concerned about my own lackluster appraisal. These aren't the kinds of pains or pleasures that have buffetted me throughout my own experience, and my recognition of the need for such stories to be told in whatever forms they choose has next to nothing to do with such a simple representation as an honest star rating.<br /><br />It's early enough in the year for me to be keeping track of the number of books read on the fingers of one hand, and while this work is nowhere near the top, I find it good to stretch my reading faculties so early on. I don't often read plays these days, and this and another work are likely the only representatives of the genre amidst my shelves, leastwise off the top of my head. I don't particularly see myself seeking out more scripts, but I'm hoping this will be ameliorated by my graduating from text to to live performance even if that should take place far further in the future than I unconsciously assume. The 21st century doesn't seem to have been to kind to plays, but that may be sufficient reason to dig the relatively buried examples out from the usual muffled demographics. A project for a time when I'm more in the mood. In the meantime, I have a growing pile of translated behemoths to pin down to my satisfaction, and such projects wait on no woman.<blockquote>
  <i>i sat up one nite walking a boardin house<br />screamin/cryin/the ghost of another woman<br />who wz missin what i was missin<br />i wanted to jump up outta my bones<br />&amp; be done wit myself<br />leave me alone<br />&amp; go on in the wind<br />it waz too much<br />i fell into a numbness<br />til the only tree i cd see<br />took me up in her branches<br />held me in the breeze<br />made me dawn dew<br />that chill at daybreak<br />the sun wrapped me up swingin rose light everywhere<br />the sky laid over me like a million men<br />i waz cold/i waz burnin up/a child<br />&amp; endlessly weavin garments for the moon<br />wit my tears<br /><br /><br />i found god in myself<br />&amp; i loved her/i loved her fiercely</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="5154962929354263170" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_128525341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128525341" />
    <a title="Marlana-Patrice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3159155-marlana-patrice"><img alt="Marlana-Patrice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263585257p2/3159155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128525341?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marlana-Patrice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marlana-Patrice" href="/user/show/3159155-marlana-patrice">Marlana-Patrice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128525341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15219005882650280720">I have seen the play version twice including the touring company with some of the original cast members like the amazing Trazana Beverley. Yesterday, reading the actual choreopoem in its entirety for the first time gave me more insight and understanding of the poets' intentions. There are moments of joy as well as sheer despair in this piece. In other words, Shange covers a wide range of colored girl emotions. Her work is also ground-breaking because of its experimentation with form and content.</span>
  <span id="freeText15219005882650280720" style="display:none">I have seen the play version twice including the touring company with some of the original cast members like the amazing Trazana Beverley. Yesterday, reading the actual choreopoem in its entirety for the first time gave me more insight and understanding of the poets' intentions. There are moments of joy as well as sheer despair in this piece. In other words, Shange covers a wide range of colored girl emotions. Her work is also ground-breaking because of its experimentation with form and content. For instance, she consistently shortened words, something that hip-hop culture does all of the time now. Considering that this work was first copyrighted back in the 1970's shows that she was probably one of the first to experiment with words and ideas in this manner. She boldly thrusts words of the street into her piece too which tells me that this well-educated woman was not afraid to tap into the lives of everyday people, especially their raw experiences. Some of my favorite poems are "Toussaint" and "Someone Almost Walked Off Wid Alla My Stuff." The former poignantly tells about first loves. While the latter is told in the voice of experienced hurt. I can totally relate to both of these arresting poems. Another way that this book is so accessible is that it draws you in and makes you have to read it in one day. It is quite short so that is easily accomplished. In sum, I know this work will remain a universal force. It has touched so many people, not just colored girls or feminists. Now that it has been transformed into a movie version, this seminal work will without a doubt touch a whole new generation of readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15219005882650280720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1006767836" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1006767836" />
    <a title="La Tonya  Jordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32053623-la-tonya-jordan"><img alt="La Tonya  Jordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501465115p2/32053623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1006767836?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="La Tonya  Jordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="La Tonya  Jordan" href="/user/show/32053623-la-tonya-jordan">La Tonya  Jordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone </span></div>

          <div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8504001869167823419">This book is so much more powerful than the movie that is made from it. This book showcases beautifully the experience of African-American females. While I never can fully understand their experience as a gay white male I feel that I was drawn into their world by Shange's words. I was able to feel their joy, pain, and suffering. This book moved me to emotions that I didn't believe a book would be able to do and now I find myself sometimes saying one of the poems to myself in my head frequently a</span>
  <span id="freeText8504001869167823419" style="display:none">This book is so much more powerful than the movie that is made from it. This book showcases beautifully the experience of African-American females. While I never can fully understand their experience as a gay white male I feel that I was drawn into their world by Shange's words. I was able to feel their joy, pain, and suffering. This book moved me to emotions that I didn't believe a book would be able to do and now I find myself sometimes saying one of the poems to myself in my head frequently about "he nearly left widda all my stuff". When a book can resonate and stay with you days after you have read it that is when you know that you have just read something either truly great or truly bad. This one is squarely in the truly great category that got me thinking about the differences and the similarities between all human beings regardless of their color. </span>

<div id="review_2575326806" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2575326806" />
    <a title="Never Without a Book" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45952189-never-without-a-book"><img alt="Never Without a Book" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556991437p2/45952189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2575326806?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Never Without a Book" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Never Without a Book" href="/user/show/45952189-never-without-a-book">Never Without a Book</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780020248910" href="/book/show/444116.for_colored_girls_who_have_considered_suicide_when_the_rainbow_is_enuf">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2575326806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17278540839390905848">This series of poems (choreopoem/monologue) pulled me into a roller coaster of emotions that I wasn’t really prepared for, whew! Seven nameless Black women, only identified by colors (lady red, orange,yellow, blue, green,brown,and purple) talk about their experiences with rape, abandonment, abortion and domestic violence. ⁣<br/>⁣<br/>Based on my knowledge of Shange and her distinctive writing style (she mimicked how real women spoke so she could draw the readers’ in to focus and listen.) I was worried tha</span>
  <span id="freeText17278540839390905848" style="display:none">This series of poems (choreopoem/monologue) pulled me into a roller coaster of emotions that I wasn’t really prepared for, whew! Seven nameless Black women, only identified by colors (lady red, orange,yellow, blue, green,brown,and purple) talk about their experiences with rape, abandonment, abortion and domestic violence. ⁣<br />⁣<br />Based on my knowledge of Shange and her distinctive writing style (she mimicked how real women spoke so she could draw the readers’ in to focus and listen.) I was worried that I would find myself struggling with pace and content. I am happy to report that this was not the case here. Her words make you understand the characters who are authentic and complex. Weaving interconnected stories of love, empowerment, struggle and loss. This is a play I would love to see in person.⁣<br /><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/p/B74aoGwgbt7/?igshid=tcbs0n300613">https://www.instagram.com/p/B74aoGwgb...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17278540839390905848" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129659452" />
    <a title="Pamela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4242366-pamela"><img alt="Pamela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587321757p2/4242366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129659452?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela" href="/user/show/4242366-pamela">Pamela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780020248910" href="/book/show/444116.for_colored_girls_who_have_considered_suicide_when_the_rainbow_is_enuf">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4242366-pamela?shelf=afro-american-women-lit">afro-american-women-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4242366-pamela?shelf=social-agenda-reads">social-agenda-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4242366-pamela?shelf=inspirational-reads">inspirational-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129659452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9898776401267715111">"for colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf" by Ntozake Shange is a powerful choreopoem that explores many different arenas: rape, sexually-transmitted diseases, unplanned pregnancy, abortion, murder, etc... It is written in a way that conveys to the reader the physical and emotional stance of the women in the play. While delving into many social topics that seem to plague all women(not just colored girls) today, Shange creates an atmosphere in which these women are m</span>
  <span id="freeText9898776401267715111" style="display:none">"for colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf" by Ntozake Shange is a powerful choreopoem that explores many different arenas: rape, sexually-transmitted diseases, unplanned pregnancy, abortion, murder, etc... It is written in a way that conveys to the reader the physical and emotional stance of the women in the play. While delving into many social topics that seem to plague all women(not just colored girls) today, Shange creates an atmosphere in which these women are made comfortable to address these issues when they would, otherwise, not want to draw the attention. Such as the poem that addresses unplanned pregnancy and abortion - "i cdnt have people lookin at me pregnant i cdnt have my friends see this dyin danglin tween my legs...nobody came cuz nobody knew once i was pregnant &amp; shamed of myself." <br />Personally, this choreopoem spoke volumes to the corners of my mind and my heart, that is, the poem and Tyler Perry's movie, "For Colored Girls" off of which this poem is based. Unlike "Precious" based on Sapphire's "Push," I did not read the book first. As a matter of fact, I'm happy that I had an opportunity to view the movie before reading. I believe it really helped a lot in that this is my first time reading a choreopoem. The characters in the movie really brought the stories and issues to life, and, as previously mentioned, these are topics that touch all women, not just colored girls.<br />I give it 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9898776401267715111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6361411251801555478">I’m grateful to Seji @theartisangeek for hosting the #blacklitchallenge and pushing us out of our comfort zones, and to Anna @never_withouta_book for highlighting this play on her feed! I haven’t read a play since school and I have never read a play that is also a poem, full stop.<br/>.<br/>Surprisingly I got on okay with this one. It was challenging but in a good way, and it made me wish I could see a version performed live on stage one day.<br/>.<br/>Shange presents us with seven women, all unnamed, referred to b</span>
  <span id="freeText6361411251801555478" style="display:none">I’m grateful to Seji @theartisangeek for hosting the #blacklitchallenge and pushing us out of our comfort zones, and to Anna @never_withouta_book for highlighting this play on her feed! I haven’t read a play since school and I have never read a play that is also a poem, full stop.<br />.<br />Surprisingly I got on okay with this one. It was challenging but in a good way, and it made me wish I could see a version performed live on stage one day.<br />.<br />Shange presents us with seven women, all unnamed, referred to by the colour of their dresses. They take it in turns to speak about various experiences faced by women of colour, from rape and domestic violence to discrimination at school and abortion.<br />.<br />A nite with beau willie brown, positive and latent rapists’ were some of the poems that stood out to me as being the most powerful. Especially the latter, as in 1975 Shange was already aware of the shifting nature of rape - from the faceless stranger in the street most women fear to the person you know, even feel safe with. But this whole piece is excellent and you should try to read it, if not see it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6361411251801555478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Janet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1421407-janet"><img alt="Janet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442438866p2/1421407.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janet" href="/user/show/1421407-janet">Janet</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48290900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18262314095977205327">I must say I read this play--or is it poetry--or is it dance--every year or two. My favorite Shange.<br/>*********************<br/>11/6/10 I'm getting ready to see the film today, so must re-read. it will be so strange to see these characters named--in the poems they're "lady in red," "lady in white" and so on... so that you develop a feel for them by their voices alone. Must remember that a film is its own work of art and not expect something it probably won't do--replicate that dream feel of the choreop</span>
  <span id="freeText18262314095977205327" style="display:none">I must say I read this play--or is it poetry--or is it dance--every year or two. My favorite Shange.<br />*********************<br />11/6/10 I'm getting ready to see the film today, so must re-read. it will be so strange to see these characters named--in the poems they're "lady in red," "lady in white" and so on... so that you develop a feel for them by their voices alone. Must remember that a film is its own work of art and not expect something it probably won't do--replicate that dream feel of the choreopoem. <br />********************<br />Loved re-reading this and glad I did before the film--my friend and I were sobbing before the opening credits even rolled--just to hear this language again! I'm not sure, and have no way to know, whether I would have loved the film so much if I hadn't been so familiar with the piece. Would I have been confused by its intense lyricism? No way to know. I thought they integrated the dream-time and word-drunkenness and tough emotionality of the play into the realism of a film just beautifully. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18262314095977205327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1109013264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109013264" />
    <a title="Melody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20797654-melody"><img alt="Melody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1376187250p2/20797654.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109013264?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melody" href="/user/show/20797654-melody">Melody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109013264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6561851484385951421">I have never seen the movie or the stage version of this, so for some reason I went into this expecting some talk about mental illness among black women (based upon the title) or black women overcoming adversity. There were some lines that I liked and some poems that I thought were particularly good, but when I read the last page I had one overwhelming thought, 'That was really overrated.' These poems read more like a bunch of little stories. And all the stories are about black women's misery, p</span>
  <span id="freeText6561851484385951421" style="display:none">I have never seen the movie or the stage version of this, so for some reason I went into this expecting some talk about mental illness among black women (based upon the title) or black women overcoming adversity. There were some lines that I liked and some poems that I thought were particularly good, but when I read the last page I had one overwhelming thought, 'That was really overrated.' These poems read more like a bunch of little stories. And all the stories are about black women's misery, pain and heartbreak. I guess it was groundbreaking to tell a black woman's story in the 70s in this fashion. To be gritty and honest about our lives. I appreciate the delicacy she took with these stories. However! Am I supposed to be intrigued and impressed with a book featuring more of the usual fiction stories of how black women's lives are so awful? I liked the diversity in the women's life experiences, but the underlying theme was the same in all of them: it sucks to be us. Kind of depressing. I wish I liked this more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6561851484385951421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zN6qdD+lei3CASD7mO+R0qduTiF0lMnMm1chhd1OKp5m3JmmV+TP521nnYhp79Ov2mv7wW/QYFFehYS/rUSxUQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Reflecting her transcendent electric voice, this searing poetry collection is filled with moving, original stanzas that speak to both Black women’s creative and intellectual power, and express the pain, sadness, and anger of those who suffer constant scrutiny because of their gender and race. Fierce and passionate, Jessica Care moore argues that Black women spend their lives building a physical and emotional shelter to protect themselves from misogyny, criminalization, hatred, stereotypes, sexual assault, objectification, patriarchy, and death threats.\n\nWe Want Our Bodies Back is an exploration—and defiant stance against—these many attacks.<\/span>\n  <a California Cooper  has proven that hers is a wholly original talent  --one that embraces readers in an ever-widening  circle from one book to the next. With In  Search Of Satisfaction, Cooper  gracefully portrays men and women, some good and others  wickedly twisted, caught in their individual  thickets of want and need. On a once-grand plantation  in Yoville, &quot;a legal town-ship founded by the  very rich for their own personal use,&quot; a  freed slave named Josephus fathers two daughters,  Ruth and Yinyang, by two different women. His  desire, to give Yinyang and himself money and  opportunities, oozes through the family like an elixir,  melding with the equally strong yearnings of  Yoville\'s other residents, whose tastes don\'t  complement their neighbors\'. What Josephus buries in his  life affects generations to come. J. California  Cooper\'s unfettered view of sin, forgiveness, and  redemption gives In Search Of  Satisfaction a singular richness that belies its  universal themes.<\/span>\n  <a       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/32677.Ntozake_Shange">About Ntozake Shange</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/32677.Ntozake_Shange"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1190764657p3/32677.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/32677.Ntozake_Shange">Ntozake Shange
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
576
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer192056272123071259">Ntozake Shange (pronounced En-toe-ZAHK-kay SHONG-gay) was an African-American playwright, performance artist, and writer who is best known for her Obie Award winning play <i>for colored girls who have considered suicide/when the rainbow is enuf</i>.<br/><br/>Among her honors and awards are fellowships from the Guggenheim Foundation and the Lila Wallace-Reader's Digest Fund, and a Pushcart Prize. </span>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
